  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2012-publication">2012-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=male-ya-author">male-ya-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=mature-ya">mature-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=lb">lb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=april">april</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer248184096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8546887834951556705"><b>4.5 stars</b> Do you believe violent offenders are the product of nature or nurture? <br/><br/>In the case of 17-year-old Jasper “Jazz” Dent, he’s got both factors working against him. Not only is he the son of the country’s most notorious serial killer, but dear old daddy even forced him to watch those grisly crimes and sometimes…more.<br/><br/>I’ve always been interested in how human beings cope with extreme circumstances, and the way children in particular can demonstrate remarkable resilience. <i>I Hunt Killers</i> sets u</span>
  <span id="freeText8546887834951556705" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b> Do you believe violent offenders are the product of nature or nurture? <br /><br />In the case of 17-year-old Jasper “Jazz” Dent, he’s got both factors working against him. Not only is he the son of the country’s most notorious serial killer, but dear old daddy even forced him to watch those grisly crimes and sometimes…more.<br /><br />I’ve always been interested in how human beings cope with extreme circumstances, and the way children in particular can demonstrate remarkable resilience. <i>I Hunt Killers</i> sets up a fascinating scenario showing how both environment and biology can contribute to certain conditioned responses and behaviors—and how an innate sense of human decency <i>might</i> be strong enough to overcome even the worst of upbringings. At least that’s what Jazz keeps telling himself. Because now that he suspects that a new serial killer is at work in his small town, he’s flashing back to memories that make him extremely uneasy. Did he help kill someone he loved without knowing it? Is he destined to follow in his father’s footsteps? <br /><br />What sets this novel apart from all the other paint-by-numbers mysteries is that Jazz is an incredibly complex, believable character. The book has been billed as “Dexter for YA” and it’s an apt comparison; Jazz is likable, relatable, and consumed by the idea that he may not be able to stop himself from doing harm to others. The story itself is engaging, with the masterfully detailed, well-researched criminology aspects related in an accessible way. The book is also HILARIOUS from beginning to end. I didn’t expect to be laughing so much at a book about a possible serial killer in the making, but it’s impossible to resist the graveyard banter running through Jazz’s seasoned, offhand narrative.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Making a duplicate key from a wax impression was an extremely useful skill to have if you were the sort of person who liked invading other people’s homes and killing them.</i>
</b><br /><br />And later, his best friend Howie earnestly asks him what his middle name is, because he’s sure that serial killers all have three names! The choice to use humor to hook the reader into the story is brilliant, and I thoroughly enjoyed being in Jazz’s conflicted and absurdly playful head.<br /><br />Despite its humorous tone and exceptional writing, however, my guess is that this is going to be an extremely polarizing book. Its refusal to look away from the often horrific nature of brutal crimes and twisted mind games will be shocking to readers who aren’t used to these kinds of details. Early in the book we’re eased into some crimes because they’re mostly told in past tense, but the later scenes definitely escalate in tension and violence, although I don’t think they really cross the line in terms of being gratuitous rather than graphic. <br /><br />If I had to quibble about anything, I’d say that Jazz’s give and take relationship with the police is something readers will need to accept, although their doubtful reliance upon him is portrayed in a fairly believable tone. And as with all murder novels, I wasn’t particularly keen on the few scenes told from the killer’s point of view. But those things are really almost incidental when the writing is nearly pitch-perfect in balancing ghoulish humor and a macabre subject.<br /><br />It’s so exciting to see YA that pushes boundaries in this way. While I confess that I'm a little uneasy about the idea of 13-year-old being exposed to this sort of information, I don’t think the book contains too much explicit material that older teens or adults already haven’t seen in other forms of entertainment. I strongly urge readers to carefully consider whether this is a subject that they want to read about, however, because this book certainly isn’t for the faint of heart. But for the right audience, this thriller will hit all the right notes for an unforgettable reading experience. Its dark, disturbing, and devilishly funny vibe is pure genius.<br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://backinthemidnightgarden.blogspot.com/2012/03/i-hunt-killers-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>. An advance copy was provided by the publisher. Recommended for mature teens and adults only.</i><br /><br /><b>ARC Giveaway!</b><br /><br />If you’re intrigued by the sound of this book, stay tuned. We’ll be giving away an advance readers copy next week on the blog!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8546887834951556705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_266835773" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/266835773" />
    <a title="Flannery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/652877-flannery"><img alt="Flannery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312843258p2/652877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/266835773?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flannery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flannery" href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA readers who like adult crime thrillers, Dexter fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=wishlist-for-dtbs-to-keep">wishlist-for-dtbs-to-keep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=arc-galley-or-first-reads">arc-galley-or-first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=young-adult-teen">young-adult-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=i-wouldnt-read-on-the-t">i-wouldnt-read-on-the-t</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-on-tour">read-on-tour</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer266835773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5520903149607777748"><a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/04/ya-review-i-hunt-killers-by-barry-lyga.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <br/>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368140i/720654._SX540_.png' width='500' height='350' alt='I Hunt Killers by Barry Lyga Chart Comparing Gory Funny Scary and Clean' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
</a><br/>(click to enlarge)<br/><br/>I love reading about and researching serial killers. There, I said it. I am perpetually fascinated by the stories that seem too far-fetched to be true. <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_Bathory' rel='nofollow noopener'>Elizabeth Báthory</a> allegedly bathed in the blood of virgins to retain her youth. <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ted_bundy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ted Bundy</a> kept the decapitated heads of his victims in his house as mementos. <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ed_Gein' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ed Gein</a> dug up dead bodies and made a belt out of nipples. This is the stuff nightmares are made of. So it was with a certain excitement that I started reading <i>I </i></span>
  <span id="freeText5520903149607777748" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/04/ya-review-i-hunt-killers-by-barry-lyga.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368140i/720654._SX540_.png" width="500" height="350" alt="I Hunt Killers by Barry Lyga Chart Comparing Gory Funny Scary and Clean" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
</a><br>(click to enlarge)<br><br>I love reading about and researching serial killers. There, I said it. I am perpetually fascinated by the stories that seem too far-fetched to be true. <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_Bathory" rel="nofollow noopener">Elizabeth Báthory</a> allegedly bathed in the blood of virgins to retain her youth. <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ted_bundy" rel="nofollow noopener">Ted Bundy</a> kept the decapitated heads of his victims in his house as mementos. <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ed_Gein" rel="nofollow noopener">Ed Gein</a> dug up dead bodies and made a belt out of nipples. This is the stuff nightmares are made of. So it was with a certain excitement that I started reading <i>I Hunt Killers</i>. Barry Lyga created a fun friendship, a believable relationship (and interracial, which is exciting to note as interracial relationships are few and far between in YA), and two pretty darn scary serial killers. One is the protagonist's father, Dear Old Dad, who killed over 120 people and is now in prison. The other is a new killer, one who just started murdering people in Jazz's own town. The locals will never forget what his father did, nor will some of them ever treat him as anything other than someone about to follow in his father's footsteps. <br><br>Jazz himself is worried about becoming a killer. He knew about a lot of his father's victims and he keeps having nightmares (or are they memories?) about helping his father kill something/someone but he can't put the pieces together. He knows the history and evidence from his father's kills in and out and believes he understands the mind of a serial killer, so when the new killer starts racking up victims, Jazz attempts to help the local police solve the crime. The chief humors him more than I believe to be likely, but the funnier parts of the novel, and it IS funny, involve Jazz and his hemophiliac best friend Howie doing a little crime-solving work on their own. A lot of humor is also added by Jazz's grandmother, with whom he lives. She has increasing memory loss and often does wacky things and mistakes people for others. Of all the points in the novel that I could've been offended by, I was a little disheartened by the fact that Jazz essentially drugs his grandmother several times to keep her sleeping. Also, in regards to his grandmother, I felt like the child services worker, though well-intentioned, was unrealistic. Anybody who has worked in or around the system would probably raise an eyebrow at a worker making such an effort over someone who is healthy, not abused, able to support himself, and 6 months from aging out of the system. Sad, but true. <br><br>Fans of thrillers and horror novels will probably enjoy this, regardless of its YA categorization. When I was trying to think of readalikes, the only thing similar in the YA genre that I am aware of is the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7617119-i-am-not-a-serial-killer" rel="nofollow noopener">John Cleaver</a> series by Dan Wells and I signed out of that series after the first book added in a paranormal element. This book had more gory elements, funny dialogue, more realism, and it was scarier. I was fully engaged for the entirety of the novel so to me, it is the clear winner. <i>I Hunt Killers</i> ends with a bang. It can stand alone but I sincerely hope that Lyga writes more about Jazz and company. Please don't leave me hanging like this, Mr. Lyga!<br><br>Thanks to Wendy Darling at <a href="http://backinthemidnightgarden.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a> for touring her ARC of this book. I loved it!<br><br>Read this review and tons of other book-related awesomeness at <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5520903149607777748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_706924552" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/706924552" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4605519-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319681755p2/4605519.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/706924552?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/4605519-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4605519-jamie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4605519-jamie?shelf=horror-suspense">horror-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4605519-jamie?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4605519-jamie?shelf=kindle-read">kindle-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer706924552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11059141124308842443">Guilty confession: When I first started this, I was not expecting much. The summary left me skeptical to a good plot but I was determined to try because I had already heard lots of great things about the sequel to this one. What I can say now is that I am so glad I did. This book is so much more than what it seems on the surface!<br/><br/> As I began, I was torn or the style in which the story was presented. At first it seemed short and abrupt. Normally this would annoy me but after the first couple chapt</span>
  <span id="freeText11059141124308842443" style="display:none">Guilty confession: When I first started this, I was not expecting much. The summary left me skeptical to a good plot but I was determined to try because I had already heard lots of great things about the sequel to this one. What I can say now is that I am so glad I did. This book is so much more than what it seems on the surface!<br /><br /> As I began, I was torn or the style in which the story was presented. At first it seemed short and abrupt. Normally this would annoy me but after the first couple chapters I was quickly captivated by the thought process of young Jasper (more commonly known as Jazz) Dent. Once you get to understand him, the style it is written in makes so much more sense and fits to his personality and lifestyle.<br /><br />This poor guy has lived a life of hell! A serial killer for a father who's victims were in the triple digits. After his father is caught is stuck with his deranged grandmother. What a crazy coot she is! He is so worried his mentality is like his fathers. He has seen WAY too much horror for his age. How can it not twist a person?<br /><br />When a new serial killer makes an appearance in his town, Jazz is determined to help solve it. To absolve himself, to clear his name or prove just what kind of person he really is no one knows. Jazz is smart and methodical but no matter how much he tries, he can never escape his father's shadow. Especially when the killers methods strike too close to home for comfort!<br /><br />I cannot express enough how much I enjoyed this. A great psychological thriller and mystery. The mental battles Jazz goes through are so well described. You really feel you are right there in his brain, working through everything with him. Jazz is terrified of his own capabilities to kill. Questioning if he has killed, figuring how easy it would be to kill... Then trying to solve the crimes and save his friends! <br /><br />This book goes through a wide range of mental processes one might experience under such a life. Almost makes you wonder about the author... (just kidding!). There is action, violence and death in this book. While it is Young Adult in nature, it is older adult. Do not let the writing style and the lighter chapters at the beginning fool you. This goes dark! It is filled with twists and turns and unexpected moments. I cannot wait to continue the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11059141124308842443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review706924552">

<div id="review_648724159" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648724159" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/648724159?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=detective">detective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=action">action</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer648724159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16071159514668533073">Actual rating: 4.5<br/><br/>A dark psychological thriller. I have to admit, this wasn't what I expected. Given the premise, I anticipated something more flimsy, something along the lines of Encyclopedia Brown, Boy Detective. I got a young Dexter/John Cleaver, with considerably more emotional baggage. This book works for me more as a psychological analysis than anything. Yeah, the plot is there, and it is good. The mystery kept me guessing and I loved seeing things through the eyes of the killer, but the p</span>
  <span id="freeText16071159514668533073" style="display:none">Actual rating: 4.5<br /><br />A dark psychological thriller. I have to admit, this wasn't what I expected. Given the premise, I anticipated something more flimsy, something along the lines of Encyclopedia Brown, Boy Detective. I got a young Dexter/John Cleaver, with considerably more emotional baggage. This book works for me more as a psychological analysis than anything. Yeah, the plot is there, and it is good. The mystery kept me guessing and I loved seeing things through the eyes of the killer, but the psychoanalytical aspects of this book blew the actual storyline out of the water. Psych 101? Please. I gained more insight into the human mind from this book than from anything I learned in that class.<br /><br /><s>Or maybe I just slept through that class. Whatever, I PASSED, OK?</s><br /><br />Jasper's father is a serial killer, the worst (meaning the best, and not the most terrible) serial killer of all time. He has killed 123...or 124, people before stupidly getting caught, and now poor Jazz is left to grow up pretty much on his own in a town where his name is notorious for being the child of a serial killer who got caught. Nobody held him accountable for his father's crimes since he is a juvenile, and not an actual accessory to his father's crimes despite the fact that his dad has been practically grooming him to take over the "family business" since he's been in action---meaning started killing people. Jasper (Jazz) is extremely intelligent for his age, he's got the street savvy, he's got the smooth-talking skills down, he's got dear old dad's skills of persuasion, and some others that he wish he didn't. Now, there's another killer loose in the town of Lobo's Nod, Jazz thinks it's a serial killer but nobody believes him, and he's out to investigate.<br /><br />Not the smartest move if you want to stay under the radar, but I suppose if he acted intelligently and kept his head low, this book wouldn't exist.<br /><br />Jazz: I loved Jazz's character, his complexity, his conflicting desires. This book is an insight into his head, the psychological torment that he goes through day by day knowing that he is his father's son. He struggles with his desires to do good and the darker parts of him that might be a little too close to his father than he likes. The conflict inside him is beautifully written. From the charismatic, normal front he puts up daily to fool others, to his deeper inner struggles with his father's programming. He's got a dark sense of humor, and I rather like that as a bit of a break within such a dark tale. Children are so impressionable, and even if his father got caught, the years and years of grooming affected his mind more than he wants to believe. He doesn't want to be like his father...who, besides the most twisted, mentally ill children wants to emulate a serial killer when they grow up---but Jazz can't help growing up the way he did, having witnessed what he did, and having the same blood running through his veins. Jazz <i>knows</i> his own terrifying potential, should he allow it to grow.<br /><br /><b>"'But you don't want to kill people,' she'd said with finality, and Jazz had let the conversation die right there. Because the only honest response would have been:<br />It's not that I want to or don't want to. It's just…I can. I could. It's like…I imagine it's like being a great runner. If you knew you could run really fast, wouldn’t you? If you were stuck walking somewhere, wouldn't you want to let loose and run like hell? That's how I feel."</b><br /><br />Jazz wants to do good, but he has to constantly fight the monster that's lurking within himself, however much he wants to suppress it.<br /><br /><b>"She was dying. Dying right in front of him, and he didn't trust himself to help her because he didn't trust his hands not to finish the job instead...She was in the full throes of cardiac arrest.<br />Jazz didn't think. He didn't torture himself. He tilted her head back and listened for breathing. Nothing. A moment of intense pleasure washed over him, followed by a revulsion so sickening that he almost threw himself headlong out the window."</b><br /><br />The insight into his life post-dad is pretty interesting, too. You know all the sicko serial killer fans? He's got that, just by being the infamous son. He's got media following him, exposing him (is that even <i>legal?</i> to show a juvenile in this circumstance in the media? Fucking Doug Weathers). He's got people wanting to give him money. He's got grieving parents contacting him for closure.<br /><br />He's got people angry at him, asking why he didn't just stop his dad. Simple: <b>"like the children of alcoholics and the victims of abuse, Jazz had been a master at compartmentalizing. That, combined with Billy's persistent brainwashing and total control, meant Jazz had never uttered a peep to anyone."</b><br /><br />The plot: interesting, but I can't help thinking JAZZ YOU IDIOT. JUST STAY AWAY. MOVE TO ANOTHER TOWN. When you're the child of a serial killer, wouldn't it be wisest to just stay out of the picture? Especially for a kid so smart, so savvy, so good at manipulating people and appearing normal like Jazz supposedly is? It doesn't make sense to me why he'd want to get so involved. Disbelief aside, the mystery itself, the procedures, the glimpses into the serial killer's work was well-done. The clues were given gradually, and that in combination with the flashes of POV through the killer's eyes makes this an excellent armchair detective novel. I was constantly guessing for the whodunnit through all the little bits and pieces given. There is gore, there is blood and torture, but it's nothing the average viewer of <i>CSI</i> or <i>Criminal Minds</i> haven't seen before.<br /><br />I liked all the characters. The villains, the cops, not everything is black and white. People grow, people change. Even Jazz himself is not immune to foolishness, regret, and hubris. My main concern before starting this book was the premise...a boy, just a boy, doing better detective work than the police themselves? I expected detectives to be bumbling fools, I expected people to compartmentalize Jazz, I epected this to be a Them against Me story. I was wrong. Everything and everyone had more depth than I expected.<br /><br />Oh, and the ending. Did I see that coming? Nope, nope, not from 10 miles away. Damn.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16071159514668533073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_304903214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/304903214" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/304903214?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Emily May by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer304903214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1692576396791124142"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Sequel, please? Now? I thought this book was really <i>really</i> good. I would have happily handed out five stars, except for the fact that I had the killer's identity figured out less than halfway through the book. I feel very sad that Ms Dense seems to have been randomly replaced with Marple, but thankfully this novel is about a lot more than just solving the main mystery.<br/><br/>I actually took longer to read this book than I tend to do, and most of that time was spent on the first few chapters. So I s</span>
  <span id="freeText1692576396791124142" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Sequel, please? Now? I thought this book was really <i>really</i> good. I would have happily handed out five stars, except for the fact that I had the killer's identity figured out less than halfway through the book. I feel very sad that Ms Dense seems to have been randomly replaced with Marple, but thankfully this novel is about a lot more than just solving the main mystery.<br><br>I actually took longer to read this book than I tend to do, and most of that time was spent on the first few chapters. So I shall be issuing a warning to those who feel underwhelmed at first - stick with this book, it really does get better and better. The problem was, depraved individual that I am, I felt the introduction to the story and characters to be really light. I'm the kind of reader who likes my mysteries dark and full of gore and psychopaths... and Jasper Dent's character reminded me of a much smarter version of Cassel from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6087756.White_Cat__Curse_Workers___1_" title="White Cat (Curse Workers, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">White Cat</a>. I love Cassel, but he never strikes me as a "serious" character, and this is how I felt towards Jasper. At first.<br><br>But it soon became apparent that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/150484.Barry_Lyga" title="Barry Lyga" rel="nofollow noopener">Barry Lyga</a> really knows how to balance light and dark in a way I'm not even familiar with. There was humour in this book and Jasper Dent was in many ways a regular teenage boy with a best friend and a girlfriend. Since his dad was arrested, he has lived with his grandmother - a woman suffering from the effects of old age and a sometimes cruelly psychotic personality - but this is all rather amusing, instead of tragic. However, the author's ability to suddenly flip the switch between light-hearted teen humour and really dark descriptions of murder and sociopathic tendencies had quite an effect on me. It could have seemed silly and forced, yet for me it just made it more dramatic and disturbing.<br><br>Perhaps this is just me because I don't recall reading reviews that have picked up on this dark twistedness. But I honestly thought there was something extremely horrifying and effective about the contrast between light and dark tones in the novel. <br><br>Jasper Dent is also a very complex character, he has all kinds of conflicting emotions flying around inside him. He is the kind of person who questions his motives for everything: is he helping someone because he wants to help them? Or is he helping them for what he gets out of it? If a person is brought up knowing only one way of life, are they destined to follow that path? Can they change?<br><br>There are a few problems I had with the story. I don't believe the sheriff would really have been that understanding in a real life situation, and I don't believe he wouldn't have been just a tad more suspicious of Jasper in the beginning. Also, would that social worker really have been that concerned for a guy so close to eighteen who could obviously look after himself? I'm not sure they would have.<br><br>These things are very small matters that don't actually take anything away from the novel. This is a seriously gripping story... so, you know what you should do: read it!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="1692576396791124142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1240779031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8179145861123117837"><br/>Jasper Dent is the most popular teenage boy in school. Wait! Not just in school but in the whole town although for the last reason you could think of. Well, he’s only the son of the most notorious killer, Billy Dent who kind of reminds me of Dennis Hopkins as Hannibal.<br/> <br/><b> *Cowers* </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433683009ra/15130411.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b> *Shivers* </b><br/><br/>Billy has been locked up in prison for four years now but somebody, a fanboy? is copying one of his serial kills as the Artist and calls himself the Impressionist. What is Jasper Dent’s role in all of this? <br/><br/>Co</span>
  <span id="freeText8179145861123117837" style="display:none"><br>Jasper Dent is the most popular teenage boy in school. Wait! Not just in school but in the whole town although for the last reason you could think of. Well, he’s only the son of the most notorious killer, Billy Dent who kind of reminds me of Dennis Hopkins as Hannibal.<br> <br><b> *Cowers* </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433683009ra/15130411.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> *Shivers* </b><br><br>Billy has been locked up in prison for four years now but somebody, a fanboy? is copying one of his serial kills as the Artist and calls himself the Impressionist. What is Jasper Dent’s role in all of this? <br><br>Could he really be set on stopping the kills or could he really be what everybody expects him to be? His father’s protégé?<br><br>This is an example of a brilliantly unique psychological thriller premise with the exact amount of suspense, affective psychoanalyses to boggle your mind all combined to create a gritty story for young adults. To me, this is almost unheard of.<br><br>What gripped me really tight to the story is the detailed presentation of Jazz’s upbringing causing the wars constantly battling inside his head whenever he has to come up with judgment of what is right and wrong. <br><br>Jasper’s crazy Gramma although most of the things she said and did were plain horrifying provided dark comic relief while his hilarious best friend, Howie [who reminds me so much of my favorite singer, Natasha Bedingfield’s I Bruise Easily (in the most literal sense)] provided the light and easy ones.<br><br>Identifying the killer was kind of easy and a bit predictable but it did not interfere with the suspense of the story.<br><br>For the author to be able to come up with an idea like this alone is already impressive.<br><br>I would really want to read the sequels but they're too long (for me) and lately I've been such a lazy reader and couldn't seem to read anything more than 400 pages. :( Someday, I hope I could.^^</span>

<div id="review_298760538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/298760538" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/298760538?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=signed">signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer298760538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10636983351846666096"><i>"A serial killer's greatest ability is the ability to blend in"</i><br/><br/>I love being in the mind of a serial killer. Is this bizarre? Maybe a little. But with an older sister at home, I skipped the fairy tales, instead I grew up watching Freddy Krueger and reading murder mysteries. Naturally, I Hunt Killers immediately attracted my interest with its serial killer's son synopsis. Then when I removed the dust jacket and saw this:<br/><br/>♫ <i>We're here for a good time!</i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373007i/726428.jpg' width='280' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>You have to admit, there is something fascinating</span>
  <span id="freeText10636983351846666096" style="display:none"><i>"A serial killer's greatest ability is the ability to blend in"</i><br><br>I love being in the mind of a serial killer. Is this bizarre? Maybe a little. But with an older sister at home, I skipped the fairy tales, instead I grew up watching Freddy Krueger and reading murder mysteries. Naturally, I Hunt Killers immediately attracted my interest with its serial killer's son synopsis. Then when I removed the dust jacket and saw this:<br><br>♫ <i>We're here for a good time!</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373007i/726428.jpg" width="280" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You have to admit, there is something fascinating about serial killers. The way they think, how they analyze and see the world. It's no secret that they're sociopaths, but in most cases they have very high IQs, making them highly interesting to study. These people are masterminds. In I Hunt Killers, being in the most notorious serial killer's son's head, we learn a lot about the ins and outs of this lifestyle. Jazz is such a captivating protagonist. He's deeply disturbed by what his father has done, not just the killings themselves, but how he has was raised - to be his protege. He doesn't want to be like his father, but is it too late? Is the damage done? It's sad and it's terrifying to be inside Jazz's head. I questioned it all as much as he did. Is he sane? Is he dangerous? His best friend Howie is quite the opposite. He's simple minded and a great supportive friend to Jazz. I adored him. Plain and simple. Together, they can be pretty amusing. I loved the added humor in this novel. It's just the right amount to give it charm, while keeping the overall plot gritty and dangerous. <br><br><i>Howie: "What if the whole thing was just an accident?"<br>Jazz: "And what? Accidentally cut off three fingers postmortem? 'Oops, oh no, my girlfriend just died! Clumsy me, in trying to perform CPR, I chopped off some fingers! Guess I'll take them with me…Oh, darn, where did that middle finger go?' "</i><br><br>I can't forget to mention his Grandma, oh lord is she hilarious. She's senile, suspected to suffer from Alzheimer's with bouts of delirium; she was never really right in the head to begin with. As you can imagine, this brings up some pretty amusing antics from her when cops and media are involved. Like crawling on the floor army-style with a kitchen knife; it's distressing, really - but her delusions are priceless. <br><br>"<i>They're gonna rape mongrel babies into me! Mongrel babies to kill white folks! And they're gonna give me the AIDS to kill me off!" Grandma ranted</i><br><br>Faint of heart? Does it bother you to think of feeding human eyeballs to a cat? You may want to steer clear of this one. Although it's considered YA, there is a fair amount of gore and plenty of blood running through these pages. Jazz can't get away from his father constantly invading his thoughts, and now he has to find the one mimicking him; the story is definitely explicit and I appreciate that Lyga didn't shy away from it. This rawness - it gives a convincing portrayal of a teenage killer's son's story. <br><br>The mystery itself is not insurmountable. There are two or three obvious choices that become quite apparent, but there is still an extra twist I didn't expect, and the bigger storyline of Jazz figuring himself out is what's at the heart of this book. The ending - exciting and alarming - opens up tons of possibilities for the sequel which I am greatly anticipating! <br><br>--<br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358334i/709537.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10636983351846666096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1977366450" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1977366450" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1977366450?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Matt by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/22371819-mariah-roze">Mariah Roze</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1977366450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4749057651167926194">After making my way through the entire collection of prequel short stories in this series, I was ready to commence the novel trilogy, armed with enough background information. Barry Lyga’s writing makes it quite easy to delve in and want to push forward until the final page, in hopes of catching all the action. Jasper ‘Jazz’ Dent has lived an odd sort of life. His father, Billy, is one of the most notorious serial killers of all times, captured by fluke a few years ago. His mother disappeared wh</span>
  <span id="freeText4749057651167926194" style="display:none">After making my way through the entire collection of prequel short stories in this series, I was ready to commence the novel trilogy, armed with enough background information. Barry Lyga’s writing makes it quite easy to delve in and want to push forward until the final page, in hopes of catching all the action. Jasper ‘Jazz’ Dent has lived an odd sort of life. His father, Billy, is one of the most notorious serial killers of all times, captured by fluke a few years ago. His mother disappeared when he was just a child, though there are hints that she might have been one of Billy’s victims. Forced to live with his senile grandmother, Child Protection Services have Jasper on their radar, as he all but raises himself. His father’s actions have made him a pariah in the small community of Lobo’s Nod, with only two friends his own age—Howie, his best friend, and Connie, his girlfriend—to help him make it through high school. When the body of a young woman turns up, the authorities are baffled, having had few deaths in the area since the last 1970s. Jasper cannot help but explore the crime scene for clues, thinking that his ‘killer mind’ could see things that the sheriff might miss. As he learns a little more about the crime and victim, Jasper continues to have horrible flashbacks to the ‘training’ his father offered him about killing and dismembering. Discovering the body of the victim has had fingers removed, Jasper knows that this is a serial killer on the loose, though no one is ready to believe him, at least until another body shows up. It is then that Jasper thinks back to all he knows about killing and victim selection. These victims ring a bell for Jasper, one that comes to him in another of his flashbacks. They follow the list of early kills by Billy Dent, which may allow Jasper to forewarn the authorities. Rather than waiting for more bodies to pile up, Jasper makes the risky decision to visit his father in prison, in hopes of learning something new. Meanwhile, in the shadows, the Impressionist lurks, looking for the next victim. Lyga spins a wonderful tale to get this series going. There is a great deal for the attentive reader to learn within these pages and this is sure to help create a real buzz for the rest of the trilogy and handful of short pieces on offer.<br /><br />A friend of mine got me interested in the I Hunt Killers series and I have not been able to put it down. The prequel short stories laid all the needed groundwork before I dove into this piece and have not been able to put it down. Exploring the life of a teenager who was raised to kill poses an interesting premise, one in which Lyga has begun a deeper exploration. Jasper Dent is surely a young man whose past is coming back to haunt him. His flashbacks and knowledge of death open the discussion of nature versus nurture when it comes to personality traits, something the reader can discover by keeping a close eye on the character development found within. Lyga has laid the groundwork for Jasper in this novel, as well as the prequel pieces, all of which comes to the surface at various points. Jasper seeks to shed the persona that has been attributed to him while also seeking to use that knowledge for good. His determination not to sit on the sidelines can be applauded, though he does flirt with danger throughout. The handful of secondary characters surely complement Jasper, particularly his closest friends. The three teenagers may have tendencies to act their age, but the story is not told in such a way as to make it seem corny or even teen-geared. There is a certain grit to the narrative, one that cannot be easily explained, though it works well to propel the story forward. The scenes are gory at times, but not explored in an overly-graphic nature, allowing a larger cross-section of the population to enjoy the book. Lyga has developed his story and characters very well and keeps the plot moving forward, including some twists near the end that will push readers to get their hands on the next novel, if only to learn more about what is going on.<br /><br />Kudos, Mr. Lyga, on an outstanding series debut novel. I am glad I read the prequel pieces first, as it enriched my reading experience, but you have done so well that I could have started here without issue.<br /><br />Love/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a><br /><br />A Book for All Seasons, a different sort of Book Challenge: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/248185-a-book-for-all-seasons">https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/...</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1056287057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12678961555069332032"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301612._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>➸ <b>
  <u>Book 2</u>
</b> : <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1240372283?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Game</a> ✬✬✬✬✬<br/>➸ <b>
  <u>Book 3</u>
</b> : <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1240372303' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blood of my Blood</a> ✬✬✬✬✬<br/><br/>The fact is, I love Dexter. Wait - I mean, early Dexter. Not the <i>I-wonder-out-loud-while-doing-the-thing-I'm-wondering-out-loud-about-</i>Dexter we're forced to stand in the end. What Dexter? Come on! See, everything is in the voice-over and <i>Oh, dear.</i> Don't get me started about the dumbest thing the show became in the end. <br/><br/>So, I loved Dexter. <b>I love everything serial-killer related. Therefore I was prepared to love this book. <u>It didn't d</u></b></span>
  <span id="freeText12678961555069332032" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301612._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➸ <b>
  <u>Book 2</u>
</b> : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1240372283?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Game</a> ✬✬✬✬✬<br>➸ <b>
  <u>Book 3</u>
</b> : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1240372303" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood of my Blood</a> ✬✬✬✬✬<br><br>The fact is, I love Dexter. Wait - I mean, early Dexter. Not the <i>I-wonder-out-loud-while-doing-the-thing-I'm-wondering-out-loud-about-</i>Dexter we're forced to stand in the end. What Dexter? Come on! See, everything is in the voice-over and <i>Oh, dear.</i> Don't get me started about the dumbest thing the show became in the end. <br><br>So, I loved Dexter. <b>I love everything serial-killer related. Therefore I was prepared to love this book. <u>It didn't disappoint</u></b>. I guess here's the moment where I must warn you that even though it's YA, this story isn't for the faint of heart because we come across some <b>really disturbing and gore scenes</b>. But then, the serial killer deal must have already warned you, right? <br><br><b>Do you think we can turn someone into a serial killer?</b> How much does our upbringing influence our actions? Can we turn our back on faith? Is faith a real deal or just a bunch of irrational fears? <b>Can we fight our interne violence lurking?</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"The killer <i>was</i> a badass. Talk about supreme confidence. Jazz couldn't help it; he sort of admired the guy.<br><i>People matter. People are real. People matter...</i>"</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301613._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>► <b>
  <u>Crime</u>
</b> : Larceny. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301613._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Indeed after a slow start, this book was such <b>a page-turner</b> that I gave into it hours long without thinking about anything else, hooked as I was. Isn't it the perfect larceny? <i>No?</i> <br><br>What? Just look at the definition. <br>✘ <i>felonious taking or stealing</i> : okay, I was completely willing. There's that.<br>✘ <i>of someone else's personal goods or property</i> : Hours of my time<br>✘ <i>valued above (for grand) or below (for petty) a specific amount (which is $100 in many States)</i> : my time is worthless, duh, meaning it's priceless. <br>✘ <i>with the intent to deprive the owner permanently of the goods or property</i>. I'm pretty sure that's permanent, except for some lucky characters of SF novels.<br><br>Now, do I regret reading it? <b>Not by a long shot</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301613._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>► <b>
  <u>Crime scene</u>
</b> : Lobo's Nod<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301613._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Here's a little village where nothing never happens. Hmm. Well. Except <i>that</i> thing - you know, the arrest of one of the biggest serial-killer of all times - <i>aka</i> Jazz's father. Okay, there's <i>that</i>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301613._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>► <b>
  <u>Motives of the crime</u>
</b> : Play with your mind<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301613._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book appears to be <b>some psychological and thought-provoking thriller</b>, as we are immerged in Jazz's somehow disturbed mind, getting an insight in the mind of that particular kid who's been raised by a monster. Of course I loved that, what do you think?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301613._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>► <b>
  <u>Suspects</u>
</b> : There's enough depth in the characters to make them enthralling and interesting to follow.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301613._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>▤ <b>Jasper <i>'Jazz'</i> Dent</b>, teenager, raised by a serial killer, who's continually afraid to cross the boundaries between good and evil. <b>Oh, man, talk about daddy issues</b>. What a tortured kid, and for reasons. Being in his head, hearing his father pieces of advices, following him while he tries to act <i>as a human</i>, to read people correctly in order to appear normal, to <i>be</i> normal, to kill no one, because People Matter guys... <b>That was fascinating to see him struggle between his desire to be good and the darkest parts of his mind who made him wonder....</b> If... If he gave in... If he let them flow... What would happen? <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"And there were the urges. The feelings. The memories. The things that he'd been taught and then forgotten, but that lurked somewhere in his brain's basement, ready to strike like stalkers in the night."</b>
</blockquote><br><i>Haunted</i> - Jasper's haunted. By this father's actions. By the way he was raised. By his fears to become a real legacy for his serial killer of a father. By this knife he can't help but see in his nightmares. Haunted. Broken in a way nobody can understand. Because he won't let them see. <br><br>Don't get fooled though : <b>Jasper is no innocent victim</b>. He's <b>manipulative</b> and flashing his mega-watt smile comes just as easily to him as breathing - he became a master of "looking normal", and has a millions expressions in his arsenal to use when needed. As his father, he's charming, handsome, and looks completely above suspicion. Actually he reminded me of Dexter in the way he has to read people to know how to act sometimes : <i>Is Connie happy?</i> Hmm, yeah, she seems to be. I mean, the girl does smile. That's a good sign right? (Little tips : that's not always a good sign). He's got also this <b>dark humor</b> I loved in Dexter, this ability to see life through a twisted glass, to see people as they truly are, free of their false pretenses... Or so he thinks.<br><br>Jasper, always on the edge of... <b>Jasper, for whom I ended caring deeply.</b> <br><br>▤ <b>Howie, best-friend</b> of sub-mentioned Jazz, likes cracking inappropriate jokes, and suffers from hemophilia. This loyal kid cracked me up something fierce.<br><br>▤ <b>G. William, State sheriff</b> - too nice to be true, but then, guilt and pity can do that to people, I've been told. <br><br>▤ <b>Connie, Jazz's girlfriend</b>, is a stronger Rita (yes, Dexter's Rita, remember?). As Jazz expresses it, she's his anchor, his human part, somehow... The one who's not afraid to tell him that this killer joke, now, wasn't the best idea he could have. Can he swear never telling it again? Yeah? Good. In my opinion she's perfect for him. <br><br>About their relationship, it seems important to mention that contrary to many YA books, the author didn't take the simplistic approach of the overwhelming romance we often find : indeed instead of creating a new romance, he chose to show us <b>the developments of an already existing relationship</b>, adding <b>more depth</b> to its treatment in my opinion. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Maybe it was a guy/girl thing.<br>He hoped that's all it was. What if it was a predator/prey thing? A <i>human</i> thing? What if he was losing his connection to her? God, don't let that be."</b>
</blockquote> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301613._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>► <b>
  <u>Evidences</u>
</b> <i>aka</i> what you must know about the plot<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301613._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✔ There's <b>a serial-killer running in the wild</b>, and Jazz's mission is to catch him. Or so he thinks. <i>Did I guess who the killer was?</i> Nope, but then, I'm all kinds of stupid with thriller sometimes, and most of the readers guessed earlier. Now, I don't think guessing would spoil the read because what's important here is the journey through Jazz's mind in my opinion. That's where this book is filled with originality. You want to read a regular investigation? Go in the bookstore, check the thrillers. There's tons of them. Will you find other Jaspers? I don't think so. <br><br>✔ I can't deny that the way police officers let Jazz investigate can appear completely <b>unbelievable</b>, being a teenager and all.<br> <br>✔ Of course we can wonder WHY in the world doesn't Jazz hide or, I don't know, <i>moves</i> in another town. Let's face it, if he did I wouldn't write this review, because there would be no book, so, well... Moreover, I really think that guilt can grandly influence people behavior, so his need to show that he's good, that he isn't like his father? That's believable to me. <br><br>✔ I developed an unhealthy crush on Jazz. Bad me. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301613._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Verdict</u>
</b> : Why, of course I recommend. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427651598i/14301613._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428077014i/14359784._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12678961555069332032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/558141616?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer558141616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4291502551273168741">This was an entertaining YA thriller. It had a nice blend of mystery, action, and suspense. <br/><br/>We followed the exploits of 17 year old Jasper Dent, son of the worlds most notorious serial killer, as he tried to help the police in his local town hunt down a copycat killer of his father. <br/><br/>The story was interesting enough. Jasper was a decent lead character. He had a horrible childhood and his evil father had taught him to be just like him and so Jasper was worried that he himself was destined to becom</span>
  <span id="freeText4291502551273168741" style="display:none">This was an entertaining YA thriller. It had a nice blend of mystery, action, and suspense. <br /><br />We followed the exploits of 17 year old Jasper Dent, son of the worlds most notorious serial killer, as he tried to help the police in his local town hunt down a copycat killer of his father. <br /><br />The story was interesting enough. Jasper was a decent lead character. He had a horrible childhood and his evil father had taught him to be just like him and so Jasper was worried that he himself was destined to become a killer. Lyga really did a good job selling that aspect of the story. The big flaw in this book was the secondary characters. I never really managed to form any sort of emotional attachment to them. <br /><br />The mystery aspect of the story was pretty well done. I never guessed the identity of the copycat killer until just before the big reveal and even then Lyga had another big twist up his sleeve that should make for an interesting sequel story! <br /><br />All in all this as an entertaining YA read. <br /><br />Rating: 4 stars. I feel like I'm being a bit generous here but this is better than a lot of the books I rate 3.5 stars. <br /><br />Audio Note: Charlie Thurston did a decent job with the audio. </span>

Not that that's a big thing or anything.<br/><br/>If you put How to Get Away With Murder, Criminal Minds, and Law-Abiding Citizen into a blender, add a dash of Psych and a teen protagonist, something like this book would be the end result.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457720875ra/18395191.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457720875ra/18395192.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457720875ra/18395193.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457720875ra/18395194.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Gory at times but also completely fascinating, like my favorite shows/movies here.</span>
  <span id="freeText9571961099859810618" style="display:none">WHAT. FRESH. HELL.<br><br>Already partway into book two. <div id="review_303361671" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/303361671" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/303361671?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stacia (the 2010 club) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=suspense-or-thriller">suspense-or-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=realistic-general-or-lit-fiction">realistic-general-or-lit-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer303361671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1143520953949616402"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373703i/727385.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>HEY. YOU WEREN'T SUPPOSED TO CROSS THE TAPE. THIS IS A CRIME SCENE INVESTIGATION.</b><br/><br/>Oh who are we kidding...no one ever pays attention to warnings, especially book characters.<br/><br/>Our lead character Jasper (Jazz) is no exception. Except in his case, he is smarter than the average <s>bear</s> cop. After all, you might know a thing or two when your dad is one of the most famous serial killers of all time. His skills are bound to come in handy when hunting down a serial killer who is copying his dad's moves.<br/><br/>Welco</span>
  <span id="freeText1143520953949616402" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373703i/727385.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>HEY. YOU WEREN'T SUPPOSED TO CROSS THE TAPE. THIS IS A CRIME SCENE INVESTIGATION.</b><br><br>Oh who are we kidding...no one ever pays attention to warnings, especially book characters.<br><br>Our lead character Jasper (Jazz) is no exception. Except in his case, he is smarter than the average <s>bear</s> cop. After all, you might know a thing or two when your dad is one of the most famous serial killers of all time. His skills are bound to come in handy when hunting down a serial killer who is copying his dad's moves.<br><br>Welcome to...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373703i/727386.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Three fingers on the right hand were missing - the index finger, the middle finger, and the ring finger. The thumb and pinky were all that remained; that hand would flash devil horns while the corpse rotted in the ground somewhere.</i><br><br>Apparently, being smart enough to catch a killer does not include knowing the difference between the "devil horn" sign and the "hang loose" sign. Ah well, I'll let that slide. Jazz is still pretty useful. <i>So what if his brain's a little fried?</i> Mine would be too if I had to watch my dad mutilate people and animals when I was a small child, and because of this I now couldn't get my father's voice out of my head.<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Struggling is what makes it worth doing, Billy said. Jazz closed his eyes, trying to chase away his father's voice, but it was no good.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>This is not an easy read. The details of the murders are startling and graphic. It's a pretty dark story. <i>I was, however, completely bowled over by this peek into a life so far out of the realm of ordinary.</i> The poor kid...everyone around him seemed to be pulling him back and forth. His father and grandmother believed him to be a monster, while his best friend and girlfriend were doing everything in their power to counteract that belief.<br><br>Even Jazz himself didn't truly know who he was. Was his father right? Was his destiny not in helping to catch the killers, but instead to become one himself?<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>It's not that I want to or don't want to. It's just...I can. I imagine it's like being a great runner. If you knew you could run really fast, wouldn't you? If you were stuck walking somewhere, wouldn't you want to let loose and run like hell? That's how I feel.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>I'm so happy that this book is going to become a series. It's going to be quite the experience to watch as Jazz figures out his own head. I like that he's conflicted. Not everything is black and white in his world.<br><br>The multiple viewpoints were especially interesting. Getting the chance to be inside of the killer's head added a bit of extra creepiness to the story. <br><br>Bonus points go for fitting in a <i>Silence of the Lambs</i> reference. The last few chapters definitely had a SotL vibe. I was digging on it.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Have the lambs stopped screaming, Clarice?" Howie said suddenly in a dead-on Hannibal Lecter impression.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Book 2 is going to be CRAAAAAAZY. I can feel it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1143520953949616402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
