    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_293951001" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/293951001" />
    <a title="Crowinator" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/283407-crowinator"><img alt="Crowinator" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604950964p2/283407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/293951001?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crowinator" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crowinator" href="/user/show/283407-crowinator">Crowinator</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of teen sleuths, psychological horror, and Criminal Minds</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=genre-mystery">genre-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=cliffhangers-ho">cliffhangers-ho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=genre-horror">genre-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=antiheroes">antiheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=favorites-2012">favorites-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=assassins-and-serial-killers">assassins-and-serial-killers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer293951001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8512279778553833271"><b>First Line:</b> “By the time Jazz got to the field outside town, yellow police tape was everywhere, strung from stake to stake in a sort of drunken, off-kilter hexagon.”<br/><br/><b>Cover Story: Night Prowler</b><br/>“I'm your Night Prowler, break down your door<br/>I'm your Night Prowler, crawling 'cross your floor<br/>I'm your Night Prowler, make a mess of you, yes I will<br/>Night Prowler, and I am telling this to you<br/>There ain't nothing you can do” – AC/DC <br/><br/><b>Five-Sentence Summary:</b><br/>Jasper “Jazz” Dent wants nothing more than to be left a</span>
  <span id="freeText8512279778553833271" style="display:none"><b>First Line:</b> “By the time Jazz got to the field outside town, yellow police tape was everywhere, strung from stake to stake in a sort of drunken, off-kilter hexagon.”<br /><br /><b>Cover Story: Night Prowler</b><br />“I'm your Night Prowler, break down your door<br />I'm your Night Prowler, crawling 'cross your floor<br />I'm your Night Prowler, make a mess of you, yes I will<br />Night Prowler, and I am telling this to you<br />There ain't nothing you can do” – AC/DC <br /><br /><b>Five-Sentence Summary:</b><br />Jasper “Jazz” Dent wants nothing more than to be left alone, but as the only son of notorious serial killer Billy Dent, responsible for over 100 brutal murders, he knows his life will never be normal. Dear Old Dad educated his son in the ways of killers, and even though Billy is in prison now, he’s still always there in Jazz’s head, whispering. That’s why when new bodies begin turning up in his home town that are eerily similar to Billy’s kills, Jazz has to clear his name early – and what better way than to catch the copycat killer himself? With his friends’ help, and with the reluctant cooperation of the selfsame detective that caught his father, Jazz investigates the murders in order to prove his innocence. If only he felt as innocent as he appears . . . <br /><br /><b>Style &amp; Substance:</b><br />Is it wrong to refer to a semi-gory psychological thriller about serial killers as a scream?<br /><br />Because this book is a scream. <br /><br />No matter how vivid the gore, how serious the stakes, or how melodramatic the angst, this is a funny book. And the funny bits don’t undercut the horror, or make it any less tense or frightening. If anything, Jazz’s breezy gallows humor gives him a likability he might not have had otherwise, being that he is constantly assessing other people as objects of manipulation and potential violence (this one looks weak and would be easy to overcome; this one I’d have to sneak up on; this one can be taken in by a megawatt smile and a friendly tone). He has moments where he is downright chilling (such as his observation that the more people are in an area, the more expendable they seem, just by virtue of their being so many of them), but cracking a self-aware joke works sort of like a defense mechanism; it’s funny but the fear and insecurity that the humor comes from makes him relatable. <br /><br />Howie, Jazz’s best friend, also provides levity with his self-depreciating wit, his goofiness, and his matter-of-fact jokes over Jazz’s family history. He’s genuinely quirky, ordering strange concoctions from the local coffee place and wishing for weird tattoos that he cannot get because of his hemophilia. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(Poor Jazz, stuck eternally with Yosemite Sam across his shoulders. The suddenly concerned adult comment from the Impressionist when he saw it cracked me up: “Don’t you think it’s time to grow up?”) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Jazz’s Gramma is also funny, though the fact that her paranoid dementia and shotgun waving is often played for laughs is troubling. But that’s what’s great about a funny, creepy book, and why I love horror comedies more than horror; spinning something that’s sad or terrible into something funny can make it that much more disturbing. It also relieves tension (all the better to shock you later, mwahaha!), a technique that Lyga uses well here. <br /><br />I thought Lyga did an excellent job telling the story from the POV of a charming but disassociated teenager, always an outsider, looking in on others as if observing a lesser or alien species. Jazz has to remind himself: <i>People are real. People matter</i>. Because when you lack empathy, you lack the ability to value other people the way you value yourself. Does Jazz really lack empathy? His internal struggle over wanting to hurt and to protect people is really well developed. Is Jazz a burgeoning sociopath with homicidal tendencies? Or is he a damaged but ultimately redeemable kid struggling to overcome his father’s brainwashing? There’s no clear answer yet, but so far it seems like Jazz has a choice. I speculate that a lot of what happens to him will hinge on his mother: recovering those lost, seriously disturbing memories, and seeing if they add up to what he’s always believed.<br /><br />Lyga does an excellent job, also, of making this a true mystery novel. It’s not obvious who the killer is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(and it’s not a random walk-in we haven’t seen before, though I like how Jazz gives a nod to that particular dose of reality – in real life, it isn’t always someone we know; it’s some random guy) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The police detective, G. William, isn’t a moron designed to make Jazz look good; he’s legitimately smart, canny, and dogged in his investigations, and his reluctant partnership with Jazz is about as believable as that sort of thing can be. There are a lot of red herrings that I feel were cleverly done, and the suspenseful scene where Jazz goes to talk to his father and ask for help just makes the puzzle bigger, rather than provide any pieces. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Oh, the sneaky bastard. I was like, Jazz, don’t move the fountain. Don’t do anything so seemingly innocuous! It’s a trick! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> That said, the reveal of the Impressionist is a little disappointing, because I wanted Jazz to figure it out (like I had) before the killer showed himself, but their showdown is tense and scary, and that moment of horror after <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ when Jazz figures out he’s been Kaiser Soze’d <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> gives it a perfect ending.<br /><br /><b>Vicarious Smoochies:</b><br />There is not much romance in this book, which is good because it would be seriously out of place. Jazz is in an established relationship with Connie, who “gets” him (or at least thinks she does), and theirs is a surprisingly healthy and supportive pairing, given that one of them is afraid to have sex in case it also comes with unsexy killing urges. Connie is a grounding force for Jazz, someone who makes him feel safe, but she also has the balls to stand up to him and call him out on “Billy-like” behavior or excessive pity-partying. I’m willing to believe that Jazz does love her (and Howie), and if he can love, than perhaps he’s got more layers than he gives himself credit for.<br /><br /><b>Mood Ring: Blood Red</b><br />There’s something entirely creepy and wrong about blood red when it’s in large doses; for example at the Seattle Public Library’s meeting room floor, whose hallways are curved and done in an endless swath of deep, dark red. (Google it to see, but know that it is much, much worse in person.) It makes the hair stand up on your arms. That’s how this book is.<br /><br /><b>Kindred Quote:</b> <br />“It doesn’t matter who my father was; it matters who I remember he was.” – Anne Sexton<br /><br /><b>Random Asides:</b><br />Gore-tastic<br />It’s a book about serial killers who torture their victims before killing them. It’s gonna be graphic. But I don’t think Lyga crosses the line into gore-for-gore’s sake; I think the gory elements are at an entirely appropriate degree. Just enough to make it seem realistic and grim and scary, but not so much that you feel like the story has devolved into an 80's slasher movie. That said, I watch and read a lot of horror and detective stories, and while I have my triggers, I might be more inured to the graphic nature of the murders in this book than the average person. (I also might feel differently if it had hit one of my triggers harder.) So be warned: this isn’t for those of you who can’t stomach your basic finger-chopping, stabby-stabby, drain-cleaner poisoning scenes.<br /><br />Murder ballads<br />In looking for the lyrics to “Night Prowler” that I quoted above, I found a whole list of <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murder_ballad" rel="nofollow noopener">murder ballads</a>. I had no idea there were so many, and that so many were so disturbing. Billy Dent should totally have a murder ballad written about him.<br /><br /><b>Read-and-Watch-Alikes:</b><br />Everyone will compare this to <i>Dexter</i>, of course, as it is the most apt. Any other crime procedural television show will also work, too, but I think <i>Criminal Minds</i> is the best example (as they deal almost exclusively with serial killers and often show things from the killer’s perspective), particularly the two episodes “Sex, Birth, Death” and “Birthright”. While <i>Silence of the Lambs</i> is a great choice, I also think this would pair well with the lesser-known movie <i>Copycat</i>, in which a serial killer expert (Sigourney Weaver – yes!) is tormented by a copycat who kills in the manner of other notorious serial killers, including the one she helped catch. <br /><br />As for books, I can think of several: <i>Hold Me Closer, Necromancer</i>, for the dark, witty tone and gory dead things; <i>White Cat</i>, <i>The Demon’s Lexicon</i>, and <i>Anna Dressed in Blood</i> for other looks into charming, dishonest, loner-like young men who realize they might be killers at heart (and who can quip with the best of them). All of them have elements of mystery, humor, and psychological horror.<br /><br />Finally, I haven’t read <i>The Killer Inside Me</i>, by Jim Thompson, yet, but it looks like a good choice for someone who wants a grittier, adult read.<br /><br /><br />OLD REVIEW COMMENTS:<br /><i>People matter. People are real.</i><br /><br />Loved it, even though I correctly guessed THA KILLAH! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Still didn't see where the ending was going, though -- Damn you, cliffhanger! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This has major series potential, as there aren't really enough teen sleuths who have the capacity to be serial murderers AND comedians as well. I loved all the characters, I loved the entirely necessary level of gore (actually, I think it was a bit tame, but I have been mainlining <i>Criminal Minds</i> for a long time), and I love that the mystery kept me guessing. If I had to come up with one criticism, I would admit that at one point I rolled my eyes Jazz's tortured self-doubt because the language he uses to express it is repetitive enough that it started to feel melodramatic, but then I was sucked back into the spell of this novel where it all felt appropriately dramatic and serious. So . . . not much criticism, then. Longer review to come.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8512279778553833271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/329145132" />
    <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine"><img alt="Mimi Valentine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314137947p2/6110599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/329145132?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi Valentine" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine">Mimi Valentine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=pure-awesomeness">pure-awesomeness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=finished-copy-for-review">finished-copy-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=best-of-2012">best-of-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer329145132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15227762524783246629"><b>Rating:</b> 4.5 out of 5 stars<br/><br/>It's hard to imagine how a serial killer's mind works. But Barry Lyga must have some sort of shady part time job or at least serial killer mind-reading powers, because this book is BRILLIANT.<br/><br/>Jazz — son of the most notorious serial killer, snarky teenager, and overall charmer — takes the phrase <i>dark hero</i> to extremes! Being brought up by his psychotic father, he has <i>How To Be A Good Serial Killer</i> lessons ingrained on his brain. Sometimes they help him figure out other cas</span>
  <span id="freeText15227762524783246629" style="display:none"><b>Rating:</b> 4.5 out of 5 stars<br /><br />It's hard to imagine how a serial killer's mind works. But Barry Lyga must have some sort of shady part time job or at least serial killer mind-reading powers, because this book is BRILLIANT.<br /><br />Jazz — son of the most notorious serial killer, snarky teenager, and overall charmer — takes the phrase <i>dark hero</i> to extremes! Being brought up by his psychotic father, he has <i>How To Be A Good Serial Killer</i> lessons ingrained on his brain. Sometimes they help him figure out other cases, and sometimes they make him seem more twisted than he is. But his dark assessments are what make him so uniquely awesome, and loving Jazz is guaranteed! ♥<br /><br />The rest of the cast is a riot too! Jazz's best friend Howie is a type-A hemophiliac and a quirky chatterbomb, which makes him the perfect sidekick to Jazz's dark-minded hero. His girlfriend Connie is a complete badass. And we can't forget Gramma Dent, whose hilarious incoherent ramblings prove that maybe being out-of-whack runs in the family.<br /><br /><b>I Hunt Killers</b> is dark. There are mentions of bodies being nailed to ceilings and eyeballs being fed to cats. But it's also surprisingly funny, with witty lines that catch you off guard. I didn't expect to be that enamoured by this book, but the serial killer logistics and chilling details had me reading into the early hours of the morning!<br /><br />Part compelling murder mystery, part intense psychological thriller, and 100 % brilliantly original story, <b>I Hunt Killers</b> is a deliciously dark novel that I would recommend to people of all sanity levels! Jasper Dent, I can't wait to learn more about you in book two! ;)<br /><br /><b>BUY or BORROW?:</b> Not only is the cover under the dust jacket bloodily gorgeous, but the story is SO wow-worthy! If you've ever been interested in how the son of a serial killer thinks, then you need to buy this book ASAP! <br /><br />(Original review at <a href="http://diminutivemimi.blogspot.ca/2012/06/review-i-hunt-killers.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Mimi Valentine's YA Review Blog</a>)</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_770948768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/770948768" />
    <a title="Spider the Doof Warrior" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2348494-spider-the-doof-warrior"><img alt="Spider the Doof Warrior" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378350294p2/2348494.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/770948768?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Spider the Doof Warrior" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Spider the Doof Warrior" href="/user/show/2348494-spider-the-doof-warrior">Spider the Doof Warrior</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer770948768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer393828363262969022">This book is full of great characters. I love Jasper. I love how strong and smart Connie is and how off the wall Howie is.<br/><br/>And man, is Jazz's dad evil. He does love his son, but dang. He's horrible! He's trying to turn Jazz into a copy of him. A serial killer like him. Jazz struggles with his messed up childhood and trying to resolve all of these issues. He doesn't want to follow in his father's footsteps. He'd rather prevent murder than be a murderer.<br/><br/>This book is a YA version of Dexter in a way,</span>
  <span id="freeText393828363262969022" style="display:none">This book is full of great characters. I love Jasper. I love how strong and smart Connie is and how off the wall Howie is.<br /><br />And man, is Jazz's dad evil. He does love his son, but dang. He's horrible! He's trying to turn Jazz into a copy of him. A serial killer like him. Jazz struggles with his messed up childhood and trying to resolve all of these issues. He doesn't want to follow in his father's footsteps. He'd rather prevent murder than be a murderer.<br /><br />This book is a YA version of Dexter in a way, but it's still gritty and actually much better than Dexter which peaked at season 4. Read this book if you like dark crime dramas, redemption and an excellent lack of race fail. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Read it again. You should read it too. Just do it.<br /><br />Still think this book is worth reading even though it is very disturbing. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="393828363262969022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_745500856" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/745500856" />
    <a title="The FountainPenDiva, Old school geek chick and lover of teddy bears" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears"><img alt="The FountainPenDiva, Old school geek chick and lover of teddy bears" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584827425p2/2142927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/745500856?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The FountainPenDiva, Old school geek chick and lover of teddy bears" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The FountainPenDiva, Old school geek chick and lover of teddy bears" href="/user/show/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears">The FountainPenDiva, Old school geek chick and lover of teddy bears</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears?shelf=author-is-my-rock-star">author-is-my-rock-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears?shelf=omg-emotional">omg-emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears?shelf=omg-provocative">omg-provocative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears?shelf=books-on-kindle">books-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears?shelf=characters-virgin-heroines">characters-virgin-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears?shelf=e-books-purchased">e-books-purchased</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears?shelf=characters-tortured-heroes">characters-tortured-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears?shelf=favourite-books-2013">favourite-books-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears?shelf=best-damn-book-ever">best-damn-book-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears?shelf=books-that-are-keepers">books-that-are-keepers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer745500856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer728075576365075124">I Hunt Killers is dark, disturbing, claustrophobic and risky. It's also a reminder of what GOOD YA fiction used to be like (with some notable exceptions) until it got dumbed-down by authors and/or publishers who seem to operate under the (mistaken) assumption that teens need to be talked down to and the stories need to be more simplistic. This is a YA novel with teeth, in turns psychologically creepy with well-placed moments of humor and humanity. Barry Lyga crafted the ultimate outsider, the so</span>
  <span id="freeText728075576365075124" style="display:none">I Hunt Killers is dark, disturbing, claustrophobic and risky. It's also a reminder of what GOOD YA fiction used to be like (with some notable exceptions) until it got dumbed-down by authors and/or publishers who seem to operate under the (mistaken) assumption that teens need to be talked down to and the stories need to be more simplistic. This is a YA novel with teeth, in turns psychologically creepy with well-placed moments of humor and humanity. Barry Lyga crafted the ultimate outsider, the son of a serial killer, and gives him a sympathy all the while prickling us deep down wondering what makes a young man like him tick (or perhaps be a ticking time bomb). Lyga also gets big kudos for diversity. The main character Jazz has a black girlfriend named Connie who is no weak-willed pushover and his friend Howie suffers from hemophilia but is found in the thick of the action with a well-placed quip. In their own ways they too are outsiders.<br /><br />Okay, serial killers are SO not my thing. Sure, I might watch the occasional Discovery ID show when bored, but I'm not into stuff like CSI or Criminal Minds. Silence of the Lambs freaked me out for a month, and the original Psycho had me so terrified as a child that I made my mom stay in the bathroom with me while I showered (I also made my folks hide all the knives). That being said, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7766027.I_Hunt_Killers__Jasper_Dent___1_" title="I Hunt Killers (Jasper Dent, #1) by Barry Lyga" rel="nofollow noopener">I Hunt Killers</a> is less about a serial killer and more about the son of one. Jasper (Jazz) Dent is a typical, good-looking teenage boy who just so happens to be the son of the most notorious serial killer in America. Talk about NOT winning father of the year awards. Jazz's childhood, if one can call it that, easily makes Mommy Dearest look like The Brady Bunch with The Waltons thrown in. Given what for all intents and purposes could be considered PTSD, Jazz struggles inside to not be a self-fulfilling prophecy. He strives for normalcy, but normalcy isn't for him, especially with a grandmother suffering from dementia whom in her lucid moments tortures Jazz mentally.<br /><br />That struggle to hold onto humanity is put to the ultimate test when a body is discovered outside of the town Jazz lives in. While law enforcement, a small police force headed by the man who brought Jazz's father to justice and saw the worst the man was capable of, doesn't notice anything too particular, Jazz knows in his gut that another serial killer is on the hunt. All the while Jazz questions his desire to find the killer as he has to think like one. Like his father.<br /><br />I just finished this and all I can really say is read this now! The writing isn't graphic or gory, but being inside the mind of brilliant and horrific madness is a journey you won't soon forget. Jazz Dent is an incredible and incredibly complex hero. I loved him, feared him and wanted to strangle him at varying points in the book. Connie is Jazz's anchor with a force of will that he needs. She sees beyond his supposedly "dark" reputation to the wounded soul inside. By the way, no race-fail here. Connie is smart, loyal and has a mind of her own. Howie is no action hero, but he doesn't allow his disease get in the way of being there for his best friend (and tattoo canvas). Barry Lyga crafted a tour de force mystery/thriller that will haunt you until the very last.<br /><br />But it's far from over...hence the title.</span>
  <a data-text-id="728075576365075124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aXVl5sinh1l2Soey2YdPi5upUCBAAAXUqfjmr9UNogRTUww0c/lOMdFhM9MuckVUTfa36I6Ni7PyhqAeGE5Qng==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xwKmVMEWSew77JOlPF8Wlv3I3Q49bNADUVMcjtgaJXX9JM+GekiAhJzHJ8TLqhxJK5c6xvPhXmQKLVo/FVnX7w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

She sees them—literally, and had been seeing the dead ever since she can remember. She tried telling her parents about it when she was a child, but they’d vehemently dismissed it to imaginary friends, so she’d stopped talking about it. There were only two people who actually knew Nonie’s secret and knew she was the real deal. One was Buggy Mouton, her best friend since kindergarten, and the other was Guy Skinard, whom Nonie considered her one true love since the day she’d laid eyes on him in high school. Buggy now worked at MeeMaw’s Café off of Main in Clay Point, and Guy, as usual, remained ever at her side—the only difference being he’d died in a freak boating accident nine years ago. Still the prankster even in death, Guy loved causing chaos, especially with men Nonie occasionally dated. She could only imagine what mayhem he might stir up while mirroring her at the funeral home and mingling with the newly departed.Only hours into the first day of her new job, pandemonium engulfs the funeral home, and much to Nonie’s surprise, it has nothing to do with Guy. It’s brought on by the family they’re serving. And when Dover’s mistress, Anna Mae Turner, shows up at the funeral home for the visitation hell’s gates rip open and Broussard’s Funeral Home suddenly turns into a geriatric war zone.Amidst the flying hairpieces, canes and curses, Nonie’s best friend, Buggy, decides to drop by the funeral home with news she can’t wait to share. A cable network in New Orleans wants to put together a paranormal investigation team and have them check out purported haunted locations in Louisiana. For every location with solid filming potential, each member of the team gets a five hundred dollar pay check. And Buggy knows without question that if anyone can sniff out the ‘restless’ dead, it’s Nonie.Knowing nothing about paranormal investigation, but lured by the sound of the adventure and the dollar signs circling through her head, Nonie agrees to become part of the Boo Krewe, the name Buggy has formally given the makeshift team.The lure of money may be one thing, but what Nonie doesn’t realize is that occasionally the dead, so excited that someone can actually see and hear them, decide to follow her home, into her bed—the bathroom—the shower. And adding to this new-found frustration, Nonie barely finishes her first investigation when she gets a visit from Anna Mae Turner—the mayor’s former mistress—now dead, as well, and harassingly   <span id="freeText8578997691476826213" style="display:none">Barry Lyga is a recovering comic book geek. According to <i>Kirkus</i>, he's also a "YA rebel-author." Somehow, the two just don't seem to go together to him.<br /><br />When he was a kid, everyone told him that comic books were garbage and would rot his brain, but he had the last laugh. Raised on a steady diet of comics, he worked in the comic book industry for ten years, but now writes full-time because, well, wouldn't you?<br /><br /><i>The Astonishing Adventures of Fanboy &amp; Goth Girl</i> is his first novel. <i>Unsoul'd</i> is his latest. There are a whole bunch in between, featuring everything from the aftermath of child abuse to pre-teens with superpowers to serial killers. He clearly does not know how to stick to one subject.</span>
